Disaster control should be undertaken when there are 3 or more hepatitis A cases. Which of these measures is a priority?
1. Eliminate faecal contamination from foods
2. Mass vaccination of uninfected individuals
3. Health promotion and education to families and communities about the disease it’s cause and transmission
4. Mass administration of Immunoglobulin
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Health promotion and education to families and communities about the disease it’s cause and transmission

What is the average incubation period of Hepatitis A?
1. 30 days
2. 60 days
3. 50 days
4. 14 days
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. 30 days

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Mrs. Pichay is admitted to your ward. The MD ordered “Prepare for thoracentesis this pm to remove excess air from the pleural cavity.”

Which of the following nursing responsibilities is essential in Mrs. Pichay who will undergo thoracentesis?
1. Support and reassure client during the procedure
2. Ensure that informed consent has been signed
3. Determine if client has allergic reaction to local anesthesia
4. Ascertain if chest x-rays and other tests have been prescribed and completed
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Ascertain if chest x-rays and other tests have been prescribed and completed

Mrs. Pichay who is for thoracentesis is assigned by the nurse to which of the following positions?
1. Trendelenburg position
2. Supine position
3. Dorsal Recumbent position
4. Orthopneic position
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Orthopneic position

During thoracentesis, which of the following nursing intervention will be most crucial?
1. Place patient in a quiet and cool room
2. Maintain strict aseptic technique
3. Advice patient to sit perfectly still during needle insertion until it has been withdrawn from the chest
4. Apply pressure over the puncture site as soon as the needle is withdrawn
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Advice patient to sit perfectly still during needle insertion until it has been withdrawn from the chest

To prevent leakage of fluid in the thoracic cavity, how will you position the client after thoracentesis?
1. Place flat in bed
2. Turn on the unaffected side
3. Turn on the affected side
4. On bed rest
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Turn on the unaffected side

Chest x-ray was ordered after thoracentesis. When your client asks what is the reason for another chest x-ray, you will explain:
1. To rule out pneumothorax
2. To rule out any possible perforation
3. To decongest
4. To rule out any foreign body
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. To rule out pneumothorax

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>A computer analyst, Mr. Ricardo J. Santos, 25 was brought to the hospital for diagnostic workup after he had experienced seizure in his office.

Just as the nurse was entering the room, the patient who was sitting on his chair begins to have a seizure. Which of the following must the nurse do first?
1. Ease the patient to the floor
2. Lift the patient and put him on the bed
3. Insert a padded tongue depressor between his jaws
4. Restraint patient’s body movement
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Ease the patient to the floor

Mr Santos is scheduled for CT SCAN for the next day, noon time. Which of the following is the correct preparation as instructed by the nurse?
1. Shampoo hair thoroughly to remove oil and dirt
2. No special preparation is needed. Instruct the patient to keep his head still and stead
3. Give a cleansing enema and give fluids until 8 AM
4. Shave scalp and securely attach electrodes to it
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. No special preparation is needed. Instruct the patient to keep his head still and stead

Mr Santos is placed on seizure precaution. Which of the following would be contraindicated?
1. Obtain his oral temperature
2. Encourage to perform his own personal hygiene
3. Allow him to wear his own clothing
4. Encourage him to be out of bed
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Obtain his oral temperature

Usually, how does the patient behave after his seizure has subsided?
1. Most comfortable walking and moving about
2. Becomes restless and agitated
3. Sleeps for a period of time
4. Say he is thirsty and hungry
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Sleeps for a period of time

Before, during and after seizure. The nurse knows that the patient is ALWAYS placed in what position?
1. Low fowler’s
2. Side lying
3. Modified trendelenburg
4. Supine
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Side lying

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Mrs. Damian an immediate post-operative cholecystectomy and choledocholithotomy patient, complained of severe pain at the wound site.

Choledocholithotomy is:
1. The removal of the gallbladder
2. The removal of the stones in the gallbladder
3. The removal of the stones in the common bile duct
4. The removal of the stones in the kidney
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. The removal of the stones in the common bile duct

The simplest pain relieving technique is:
1. Distraction
2. Deep breathing exercise
3. Taking aspirin
4. Positioning
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Positioning

Which of the following statement on pain is TRUE?
1. Culture and pain are not associated
2. Pain accompanies acute illness
3. Patient’s reaction to pain Varies
4. Pain produces the same reaction such as groaning and moaning
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Patient’s reaction to pain Varies

In pain assessment, which of the following condition is a more reliable indicator?
1. Pain rating scale of 1 to 10
2. Facial expression and gestures
3. Physiological responses
4. Patients description of the pain sensation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Patients description of the pain sensation

When a client complains of pain, your initial response is:
1. Record the description of pain
2. Verbally acknowledge the pain
3. Refer the complaint to the doctor
4. Change to a more comfortable position
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Verbally acknowledge the pain

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>You are assigned at the surgical ward and clients have been complaining of post pain at varying degrees. Pain as you know, is very subjective.

A one-day postoperative abdominal surgery client has been complaining of severe throbbing abdominal pain described as 9 in a 1-10 pain rating. Your assessment reveals bowel sounds on all quadrants and the dressing is dry and intact. What nursing intervention would you take?
1. Medicate client as prescribed
2. Encourage client to do imagery
3. Encourage deep breathing and turning
4. Call surgeon stat
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Medicate client as prescribed

Pentoxidone 5 mg IV every 8 hours was prescribed for post abdominal pain. Which will be your priority nursing action?
1. Check abdominal dressing for possible swelling
2. Explain the proper use of PCA to alleviate anxiety
3. Avoid overdosing to prevent dependence/tolerance
4. Monitor VS, more importantly RR
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Monitor VS, more importantly RR

The client complained of abdominal distention and pain. Your nursing intervention that can alleviate pain is:
1. Instruct client to go to sleep and relax
2. Advice the client to close the lips and avoid deep breathing and talking
3. Offer hot and clear soup
4. Turn to sides frequently and avoid too much talking
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Turn to sides frequently and avoid too much talking

Surgical pain might be minimized by which nursing action in the O.R.
1. Skill of surgical team and lesser manipulation
2. Appropriate preparation for the scheduled procedure
3. Use of modern technology in closing the wound
4. Proper positioning and draping of clients
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Appropriate preparation for the scheduled procedure

Inadequate anesthesia is said to be one of the common cause of pain both in intra and post op patients. If General anesthesia is desired, it will involve loss of consciousness. Which of the following are the 2 general types of GA?
1. Epidural and Spinal
2. Subarachnoid block and Intravenous
3. Inhalation and Regional
4. Intravenous and Inhalation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Intravenous and Inhalation

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Nurse’s attitudes toward the pain influence the way they perceive and interact with clients in pain.

Nurses should be aware that older adults are at risk of underrated pain. Nursing assessment and management of pain should address the following beliefs EXCEPT:
1. Older patients seldom tend to report pain than the younger ones
2. Pain is a sign of weakness
3. Older patients do not believe in analgesics, they are tolerant
4. Complaining of pain will lead to being labeled a ‘bad’ patient
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Complaining of pain will lead to being labeled a ‘bad’ patient

Nurses should understand that when a client responds favorably to a placebo, it is known as the ‘placebo effect’. Placebos do not indicate whether or not a client has:
1. Conscience
2. Disease
3. Real pain
4. Drug tolerance
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Real pain

You are the nurse in the pain clinic where you have client who has difficulty specifying the location of pain. How can you assist such client?
1. The pain is vague
2. By charting-it hurts all over
3. Identify the absence and presence of pain
4. As the client to point to the painful are by just one finger
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. As the client to point to the painful are by just one finger

What symptom, more distressing than pain, should the nurse monitor when giving opioids especially among elderly clients who are in pain?
1. Forgetfulness
2. Drowsiness
3. Constipation
4. Allergic reactions like pruritis
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Allergic reactions like pruritis

Physical dependence occurs in anyone who takes opiods over a period of time. What do you tell a mother of a ‘dependent’ when asked for advice?
1. Start another drug and slowly lessen the opioid dosage
2. Indulge in recreational outdoor activities
3. Isolate opioid dependent to a restful resort
4. Instruct slow tapering of the drug dosage and alleviate physical withdrawal symptoms
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Instruct slow tapering of the drug dosage and alleviate physical withdrawal symptoms

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Maintenance of sterility is an important function a nurse should perform in any OR setting.

Which of the following is true with regards to sterility?
1. Sterility is time related, items are not considered sterile after a period of 30 days of being not used.
2. For 9 months, sterile items are considered sterile as long as they are covered with sterile muslin cover and stored in a dust proof covers.
3. Sterility is event related, not time related.
4. For 3 weeks, items double covered with muslin are considered sterile as long as they have undergone the sterilization process
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Sterility is event related, not time related

Two organizations endorsed that sterility are affected by factors other than the time itself, these are:
1. The PNA and the PRC
2. The AORN and JCAHO
3. The ORNAP and MCNAP
4. The MMDA and DILG
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. The AORN and JCAHO

All of these factors affect the sterility of the OR equipment, these are the following except:
1. The material used for packaging
2. The handling of the materials as well as its transport
3. Storage
4. The chemical or process used in sterilizing the material
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The chemical or process used in sterililzing the material

When you say sterile, it means:
1. The material is clean
2. The material as well as the equipment are sterilized and had undergone a rigorous sterilization process
3. There is a black stripe on the paper indicator
4. The material has no microorganism nor spores present that might cause an infection
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The material has no microorganism nor spores present that might cause an infection

In using liquid sterilizer versus autoclave machine, which of the following is true?
1. Autoclave is better in sterilizing OR supplies versus liquid sterilizer
2. They are both capable of sterilizing the equipment, however, it is necessary to soak supplies in the liquid sterilizer for a longer period of time
3. Sharps are sterilized using autoclave and not Cidex
4. If liquid sterilizer is used, rinsing it before using is not necessary
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. They are both capable of sterilizing the equipments, however, it is necessary to soak supplies in the liquid sterilizer for a longer period of time

%% np3-4 %%
The nurse is going to replace the Pleur-O-Vac attached to the client with a small, persistent left upper lobe pneumothorax with a Heimlich Flutter Valve. Which of the following is the best rationale for this?
1. Promote air and pleural drainage
2. Prevent kinking of the tube
3. Eliminate the need for a dressing
4. Eliminate the need for a water-seal drainage
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The Heimlich futter valve has a one-way valve that allows air and fuid to drain. Underwater seal drainage is not necessary. This can be connected to a drainage bag for the patient’s mobility. The absence of a long drainage tubing and the presence of a one-way valve promote effective therapy

The client with acute pancreatitis and fuid volume defcit is transferred from the ward to the ICU. Which of the following will alert the nurse?
1. Decreased pain in the fetal position
2. Urine output of 35mL/hr
3. CVP of 12 mmHg
4. Cardiac output of 5L/min
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. C = the normal CVP is 0-8 mmHg. This value refects hypervolemia. The right ventricular function of this client refects fuid volume overload, and the physician should be notifed.

The nurse in the morning shift is making rounds in the ward. The nurse enters the client’s room and found the client in discomfort condition. The client complains of stiffness in the joints. To reduce the early morning stiffness of the joints of the client,the nurse can encourage the client to:
1. Sleep with a hot pad
2. Take to aspirins before arising, and wait 15 minutes before attempting locomotion
3. Take a hot tub bath or shower in the morning
4. Put joints through passive ROM before trying to move them actively
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. A hot tub bath or shower in the morning helps many patients limber up and reduces the symptoms of early morning stiffness. Cold and ice packs are used to a lesser degree, though some clients state that cold decreases localized pain, particularly during acute attacks.

The nurse is planning of care to a client with peptic ulcer disease. To avoid the worsening condition of the client, the nurse should carefully plan the diet of the client. Which of the following will be included in the diet regime of the client?
1. Eating mainly bland food and milk or dairy products
2. Reducing intake of high-fber foods
3. Eating small, frequent meals and a bedtime snack
4. Eliminating intake of alcohol and coffee
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. These substances stimulate the production of hydrochloric acid, which is detrimental in peptic ulcer disease.

The physician has given instruction to the nurse that the client can be ambulated on crutches, with no weight bearing on the affected limb. The nurse is aware that the appropriate crutch gait for the nurse to teach the client would be:
1. Tripod gait
2. Two-point gait
3. Four-point gait
4. Three-point gait
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The three-point gait is appropriate when weight bearing is not allowed on the affected limb. The swing-to and swing-through crutch gaits may also be used when only one leg can be used for weight bearing

The client is transferred to the nursing care unit from the operating room after a transurethral resection of the prostate. The client is complaining of pain in the abdomen area. The nurse suspects of bladder spasms, which of the following is the best nursing action to minimize the pain felt by the client?
1. Advising the client not to urinate around catheter
2. Intermittent catheter irrigation with saline
3. Giving prescribed narcotics every 4 hour
4. Repositioning catheter to relieve pressure
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. The client needs to be told before surgery that the catheter causes the urge to void. Attempts to void around the catheter cause the bladder muscles to contract and result in painful spasms.

A client is diagnosed with peptic ulcer. The nurse caring for the client expects the physician to order which diet?
1. NPO
2. Small feedings of bland food
3. A regular diet given frequently in small amounts
4. Frequent feedings of clear liquids
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Bland feedings should be given in small amounts on a frequent basis to neutralize the hydrochloric acid and to prevent overload

The nurse is going to insert a Miller-Abbott tube to the client. Before insertion of the tube, the balloon is tested for patency and capacity and then defated. Which of the following nursing measure will ease the insertion to the tube?
1. Positioning the client in Semi-Fowler’s position
2. Administering a sedative to reduce anxiety
3. Chilling the tube before insertion
4. Warming the tube before insertion
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Chilling the tube before insertion assists in relieving some of the nasal discomfort. Water-soluble lubricants along with viscous lidocaine (Xylocaine) may also be used. It is usually only lightly lubricated before insertion

The physician ordered a low-sodium diet to the client. Which of the following food will the nurse avoid to give to the client?
1. Orange juice.
2. Whole milk.
3. Ginger ale.
4. Black coffee.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Whole milk should be avoided to include in the client’s diet because it has 120 mg of sodium in 8 0z of milk.

Mr. Bean, a 70-year-old client is admitted in the hospital for almost one month. The nurse understands that prolonged immobilization could lead to decubitus ulcers. Which of the following would be the least appropriate nursing intervention in the prevention of decubitus?
1. Giving backrubs with alcohol
2. Use of a bed cradle
3. Frequent assessment of the skin
4. Encouraging a high-protein diet
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Alcohol is extremely drying and contributes to skin break down. An emollient lotion should be used.

The physician prescribed digoxin 0.125 mg PO qd to a client and instructed the nurse that the client is on high-potassium diet. High potassium foods are recommended in the diet of a client taking digitalis preparations because a low serum potassium has which of the following effects?
1. Potentiates the action of digoxin
2. Promotes calcium retention
3. Promotes sodium excretion
4. Puts the client at risk for digitalis toxicity
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Potassium infuences the excitability of nerves and muscles. When potassium is low and the client is on digoxin, the risk of digoxin toxicity is increased.

The nurse is caring for a client who is transferred from the operating room for pneumonectomy. The nurse knows that immediately following pneumonectomy; the client should be in what position?
1. Supine on the unaffected side
2. Low-Fowler’s on the back
3. Semi-Fowler’s on the affected side
4. Semi-Fowler’s on the unaffected side
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. This position allows maximum expansion, ventilation, and perfusion of the remaining lung.

A client is placed on digoxin, high potassium foods are recommended in the diet of the client. Which of the following foods willthe nurse give to the client?
1. Whole grain cereal, orange juice, and apricots
2. Turkey, green bean, and Italian bread
3. Cottage cheese, cooked broccoli, and roast beef
4. Fish, green beans and cherry pie
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. These foods are high in potassium

The nurse is assigned to care to a client who undergone thyroidectomy. What nursing intervention is important during the immediate postoperative period following a thyroidectomy?
1. Assess extremities for weakness and faccidity
2. Support the head and neck during position changes
3. Position the client in high Fowler’s
4. Medicate for restlessness and anxiety
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Stress on the suture line should be avoided. Prevent fexion or hyperextension of the neck, and provide a small pillow under thehead and neck. Neck muscles have been affected during a thyroidectomy, support essential for comfort and incisional support.

What would be the recommended diet the nurse will implement to a client with burns of the head, face, neck and anterior chest?
1. Serve a high-protein, high-carbohydrate diet
2. Encourage full liquid diet
3. Serve a high-fat diet, high-fber diet
4. Monitor intake to prevent weight gain
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. A positive nitrogen balance is important for meeting metabolic needs, tissue repair, and resistance to infection. Caloric goals may be as high as 5000 calories per day.

A client with multiple fractures of both lower extremities is admitted for 3 days ago and is on skeletal traction. The client is complaining of having difculty in bowel movement. Which of the following would be the most appropriate nursing intervention?
1. Administer an enema
2. Perform range-of-motion exercise to all extremities
3. Ensure maximum fuid intake (3000ml/day)
4. Put the client on the bedpan every 2 hours
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. The best early intervention would be to increase fuid intake, because constipation is common when activity is decreased or usual routines have been interrupted.

John is diagnosed with Addison’s disease and admitted in the hospital. What would be the appropriate nursing care for John?
1. Reducing physical and emotional stress
2. Providing a low-sodium diet
3. Restricting fuids to 1500ml/day
4. Administering insulin-replacement therapy
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Because the client’s ability is to react to stress is decreased, maintaining a quiet environment becomes A nursing priority. Dehydration is a common problem in Addison’s disease, so close observation of the client’s hydration level is crucial. To promote optimal hydration and sodium intake, fuid intake is increased, particularly fuid containing electrolytes, such as broths, carbonated beverages, and juices.

Mr. Smith is scheduled for an above-the-knee amputation. After the surgery he was transferred to the nursing care unit. The nurse assigned to him knows that 72 hours after the procedure the client should be positioned properly to prevent contractures. Which of the following is the best position to the client?
1. Side-lying, alternating left and right sides
2. Sitting in a reclining chair twice a day
3. Lying on abdomen several times daily
4. Supine with stump elevated at least 30 degrees
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. At about 48-72 hours, the client must be turned onto the abdomen to prevent fexion contractures.

A client is scheduled to have an inguinal herniorraphy in the outpatient surgical department. The nurse is providing health teaching about post surgical care to the client. Which of the following statement if made by the client would refect the need for more teaching?
1. “I should call the physician if I have a cough or cold before surgery”
2. “I will be able to drive soon after surgery”
3. “I will not be able to do any heavy lifting for 3-6 weeks after surgery”
4. “I should support my incision if I have to cough or turn”
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. The client should not drive for 2 weeks after surgery to avoid stress on the incision. This refects a need for additional teaching.

Ms Jones is brought to the emergency room and is complaining of muscle spasms, numbness, tremors and weakness in the arms and legs. The client was diagnosed with multiple sclerosis. The nurse assigned to Ms. Jones is aware that she has to prevent fatigue to the client to alleviate the discomfort. Which of the following teaching is necessary to prevent fatigue?
1. Avoid extremes in temperature
2. Install safety devices in the home
3. Attend support group meetings
4. Avoid physical exercise
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Extremes in heat and cold will exacerbate symptoms. Heat delays transmission of impulses and increases fatigue.

Mr. Stewart is in sickle cell crisis and complaining pain in the joints and difculty of breathing. On the assessment of the nurse, his temperature is 38.1 ºC. The physician ordered Morphine sulfate via patient-controlled analgesia (PCA), and oxygen at 4L/min. A priority nursing diagnosis to Mr. Stewart is risk for infection. A nursing intervention to assist in preventing infection is:
1. Using standard precautions and medical asepsis
2. Enforcing a “no visitors” rule
3. Using moist heat on painful joints
4. Monitoring a vital signs every 2 hour
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Vigilant implementation of standard precautions and medical asepsis is an effective means of preventing infection

Mrs. Maupin is a professor in a prestigious university for 30 years. After lecture, she experience blurring of vision and tiredness. Mrs. Maupin is brought to the emergency department. On assessment, the nurse notes that the blood pressure of the client is 139/90. Mrs. Maupin has been diagnosed with essential hypertension and placed on medication to control her BP. Which potential nursing diagnosis will be a priority for discharge teaching?
1. Sleep Pattern disturbance
2. Impaired physical mobility
3. Noncompliance
4. Fluid volume excess
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Noncompliance is a major problem in the management of chronic disease. In hypertension, the client often does not feel ill and thus does not see a need to follow a treatment regimen.

Following a needle biopsy of the kidney, which assessment is an indication that the client is bleeding?
1. Slow, irregular pulse
2. Dull, abdominal discomfort
3. Urinary frequency
4. Throbbing headache
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. An accumulation of blood from the kidney into the abdomen would manifest itself with these symptoms

A client with acute bronchitis is admitted in the hospital. The nurse assigned to the client is making a plan of care regarding expectoration of thick sputum. Which nursing action is most effective?
1. Place the client in a lateral position every 2 hour
2. Splint the patient’s chest with pillows when coughing
3. Use humifed oxygen
4. Offer fuids at regular intervals
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Fluids liquefy secretions and therefore make it easier to expectorate

The nurse is going to assess the bowel sound of the client. For accurate assessment of the bowel sound, the nurse should listen for at least:
1. 5 minutes
2. 60 seconds
3. 30 seconds
4. 2 minutes
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Physical assessment guidelines recommend listening for atleast 2 minutes in each quadrant (and up to 5 minutes, not at least 5 minutes).

The nurse encourages the client to wear compression stockings. What is the rationale behind in using compression stockings?
1. Compression stockings promote venous return
2. Compression stockings divert blood to major vessels
3. Compression stockings decreases workload on the heart
4. Compression stockings improve arterial circulation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Compression stockings promote venous return and prevent peripheral pooling.

Mr. Whitman is a stroke client and is having difculty in swallowing. Which is the best nursing intervention is most likely to assist the client?
1. Placing food in the unaffected side of the mouth
2. Increasing fber in the diet
3. Asking the patient to speak slowly
4. Increasing fuid intake
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Placing food in the unaffected side of the mouth assists in the swallowing process because the client has sensation on that side and will have more control over the swallowing process.

Following nephrectomy, the nurse closely monitors the urinary output of the client. Which assessment fnding is an early indicator of fuid retention in the postoperative period?
1. Periorbital edema
2. Increased specifc gravity of urine
3. A urinary output of 50mL/hr
4. Daily weight gain of 2 lb or more
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Daily weights are taken following nephrectomy. Daily increases of 2 lb or more are indicative of fuid retention and should be reported to the physician. Intake and output records may also refect this imbalance.

A nurse is completing an assessment to a client with cirrhosis. Which of the following nursing assessment is important to notify the physician?
1. Expanding ecchymosis
2. Ascites and serum albumin of 3.2 g/dl
3. Slurred speech
4. Hematocrit of 37% and hemoglobin of 12g/dl
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Clients with cirrhosis have already coagulation due to thrombocytopenia and vitamin K defciency. This could be a sign of bleeding

Mr. Park is 32-year-old, a badminton player and has a type 1 diabetes mellitus. After the game, the client complains of becoming diaphoretic and light-headedness. The client asks the nurse how to avoid this reaction. The nurse will recommend to:
1. Allow plenty of time after the insulin injection and before beginning the match
2. Eat a carbohydrate snack before and during the badminton match
3. Drink plenty of fuids before, during, and after bed time
4. Take insulin just before starting the badminton match
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Exercise enhances glucose uptake, and the client is at risk for an insulin reaction. Snacks with carbohydrates will help.

A client is rushed to the emergency room due to serious vehicle accident. The nurse is suspecting of head injury. Which of the following assessment fndings would the nurse report to the physician?
1. CVP of 5mmHa
2. Glasgow Coma Scale score of 13
3. Polyuria and dilute urinary output
4. Insomnia
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. These are symptoms of diabetes insipidus. The patient can become hypovolemic and vasopressin may reverse the Polyuria.

Mrs. Moore, 62-year-old, with diabetes is in the emergency department. She stepped on a sharp sea shells while walking barefoot along the beach. Mrs. Moore did not notice that the object pierced the skin until later that evening. What problem does the client most probably have?

2. Macroangiopathy
3. Carpal tunnel syndrome
4. Peripheral neuropathy
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Peripheral neuropathy refers to nerve damage of the hands and feet. The client did not notice that the object pierced the skin.

A client with gangrenous foot has undergone a below-knee amputation. The nurse in the nursing care unit knows that the priority nursing intervention in the immediate post operative care of this client is:
1. Elevate the stump on a pillow for the first 24 hours
2. Encourage use of trapeze
3. Position the client prone periodically
4. Apply a cone-shaped dressing
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. The elevation of the stump on a pillow for the first 24 hours decreases edema and increases venous return.

2. Keep the client on bed rest
3. Keep the patient on bed rest
4. Give a stat dose of Sucralfate (Carafate)
>[!FAQ]- Answer

The nurse is providing a discharge instruction about the prevention of urinary stasis to a client with frequent bladder infection. Which of the following will the nurse include in the instruction?
1. Drink 3-4 quarts of fuid every day
2. Empty the bladder every 2-4 hours while awake
3. Encourage the use of coffee, tea, and colas for their diuretic effect
4. Teach Kegel exercises to control bladder fow
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Avoiding stasis of urine by emptying the bladder every 2-4 hours will prevent overdistention of the bladder and future urinary tract infections.

A client with AIDS is admitted in the hospital. He is receiving intravenous therapy. Which action will the nurse take to remove the blood spill?

2. Promptly clean up the blood spill with full-strength antimicrobial cleaning solution
3. Immediately mop the foor with boiling water
4. Allow the blood to dry before cleaning to decrease the possibility of cross-contamination
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. A 1:10 solution of household bleach and water is recommended by the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention to kill the human immunodefciency virus (HIV).

Before surgery, the physician ordered pentobarbital sodium (Nembutal) for the client to sleep. The night before the scheduled surgery, the nurse gave the pre-medication. One hour later the client is still unable to sleep. The nurse review the client’s chart and note the physician’s prescription with an order to repeat. What should the nurse do next?
1. Rub the client’s back until relaxed
2. Prepare a glass of warm milk
3. Give the second dose of pentobarbital sodium
4. Explore the client’s feelings about surgery
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Given the data, presurgical anxiety is suspected. The client needs an opportunity to talk about concerns related to surgery before further actions (which may mask the anxiety).

The nurse on the night shift is making rounds in the nursing care unit. The nurse is about to enter to the client’s room when a ventilator alarm sounds, what is the first action the nurse should do?
1. Assess the lung sounds
2. Suction the client right away
3. Look at the client
4. Turn and position the client
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. A quick look at the client can help identify the type and cause of the ventilator alarm. Disconnection of the tube from the ventilator, bronchospasm, and anxiety are some of the obvious reasons that could trigger an alarm.

What effective precautions should the nurse use to control the transmission of methicillin-resistant Staphylococcus aureus (MRSA)?
1. Use gloves and handwashing before and after client contact
2. Do nasal cultures on healthcare providers
3. Place the client on total isolation
4. Use mask and gown during care of the MRSA client
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Contact isolation has been advised by the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC) to control transmission of MRSA, which includes gloves and handwashing.

The postoperative gastrectomy client is scheduled for discharge. The client asks the nurse, “When I will be allowed to eat three meals a day like the rest of my family?”. The appropriate nursing response is:
1. “You will probably have to eat six meals a day for the rest of your life.”
2. “Eating six meals a day can be a bother, can’t it?”
3. “Some clients can tolerate three meals a day by the time they leave the hospital. Maybe it will be a little longer for you.”
4. “ It varies from client to client, but generally in 6-12 months most clients can return to their previous meal patterns”
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. In response to the question of the client, the nurse needs to provide brief, accurate information. Some clients who have had gastrectomies are able to tolerate three meals a day before discharge from the hospital. However, for the majority of clients, it takes 6-12 months before their surgically reduced stomach has stretched enough to accommodate a larger meal.

3. “It’s probably because you have been less physically active”
4. “Your liver is not destroying estrogen hormones that all men produce”
>[!FAQ]- Answer

A client is diagnosed with detached retina and scheduled for surgery. Preoperative teaching of the nurse to the client includes:
1. No eye pain is expected postoperatively
2. Semi-fowler’s position will be used to reduce pressure in the eye.
3. Eye patches may be used postoperatively
4. Return of normal vision is expected following surgery
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Use of eye patches may be continued postoperatively, depending on surgeon preference. This is done to achieve >90% success rate of the surgery.

A 70-year-old client is brought to the emergency department with a caregiver. The client has manifestations of anorexia, wasting of muscles and multiple bruises. What nursing interventions would the nurse implement?
1. Talk to the client about the caregiver and support system
2. Complete a gastrointestinal and neurological assessment
3. Check the lab data for serum albumin, hematocrit and hemoglobin
4. Complete a police report on elder abuse
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Assessment and more data collection are needed. The client may have gastrointestinal or neurological problems that account for the symptoms. The anorexia could result from medications, poor dentition, or indigestion, the bruises may be attributed to ataxia, frequent falls, vertigo, or medication.

A nurse is providing a discharge instruction to the client about the self-catheterization at home. Which of the following instructions would the nurse include?
1. Wash the catheter with soap and water after each use
2. Lubricate the catheter with Vaseline
3. Perform the Valsalva maneuver to promote insertion
4. Replace the catheter with a new one every 24 hour
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. The catheter should be washed with soap and water after withdrawal and placed in a clean container. It can be reused until it is too hard or too soft for insertion. Self-care, prevention of complications, and cost-effectiveness are important in home management.

The nurse in the nursing care unit is assigned to care to a client who is Immunocompromised. The client tells the nurse that his chest is painful and the blisters are itchy. What would be the nursing intervention to this client?

3. Clarify if the client is on a new medication
4. Use gown and gloves while assessing the lesions
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The client may have herpes zoster (shingles), a viral infection. The nurse should use standard precautions in assessing the lesions. Immunocompromised clients are at risk for infection.

A client is admitted and has been diagnosed with bacterial (meningococcal) meningitis. The infection control registered nurse visits the staff nurse caring to the client. What statement made by the nurse refects an understanding of the management of this client?
1. speech pattern may be altered

3. Perform skin culture on the macular popular rash
4. Expect abnormal general muscle contractions
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. After a minimum of 24 hours of IV antibiotics, the client is no longer considered communicable. Evaluation of the nurse’s knowledge is needed for safe care and continuity of care.

A 18-year-old male client had sustained a head injury from a motorbike accident. It is uncertain whether the client may have minimal but permanent disability. A client with AIDS is scheduled for discharge. The client tells the nurse that one of his hobbies at home is gardening. What will be the discharge instruction of the nurse to the client knowing that the client is prone to toxoplasmosis?
1. Wash all vegetables before cooking
2. Wear gloves when gardening
3. Wear a mask when travelling to foreign countries
4. Avoid contact with cats and birds
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Toxoplasmosis is an opportunistic infection and a parasite of birds and mammals. The oocysts remain infectious in moist soil for about 1 year.

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Diabetes Mellitus is the most common endocrine disorder that accounts for the majority of non traumatic amputation as well as the third leading cause of death by disease.

Who among the following has the highest risk in acquiring diabetes mellitus?

2. Gary, 42 year old, with a Diabetic mother
3. Jonathan, 21 year old, Asian, with a diabetic mother and a sister with diabetes
4. Chris, 48 year old with a BMI of 30

>4. Chris, 48 year old with a BMI of 30

Which of the following is TRUE with regards to the TYPE 1 diabetes mellitus?
1. It accounts for the majority of Diabetes
2. All clients with Type 1 DM has an absolute lack of insulin
3. The insulin producing pancreatic beta cells produces NO or LITTLE insulin
4. Diet, Exercise and OHA are the treatment of choice
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. The insulin producing pancreatic beta cells produces NO or LITTLE insulin

1. Ketosis is common
2. Usually thin at diagnosis with recent weight loss
3. Onset is usually at the early 20s
4. There is no islet cells antibodies
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. There is no islet cells antibodies

1. 70 mg/dl
2. 140 mg/dl
3. 200 mg/dl
4. 800 mg/dl
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. 200 mg/dl

1. Metabolic Acidosis
2. Metabolic Alkalosis
3. Respiratory Acidosis
4. Respiratory Alkalosis

1. Exercise
2. Balance Diet
3. Insulin
4. OHA

>3. Insulin

While in Type 2 Diabetes, the primary treatment is:
1. Weight loss
2. Exercise
3. OHA
4. Insulin

3. Urine

3. Restlessness, irritability and generalized weakness

1. Pre renal
2. Post renal

>2. Strictly follow the hemodialysis schedule

>You are going to apply various medications

1. Directly onto the cornea
2. Into the outer third of the lower conjunctival sac
3. Pressing on the lacrimal duct

1. Squeeze about 2 cm of ointment and gently close but not squeeze the eye

If you are to give 2 nasal inhalation for a client, one is a bronchodilator and the other one is a steroid, which guideline should you follow?
1. Administer the steroid first, this is to open the airway by lessening the edema
2. Administer the bronchodilator first, this is to relax the bronchial muscle and dilate the airway
3. Order is not necessary in administering nasal inhalation as long as that the nurse will wait 1 minute between administrations of 2 drugs
4. Order is not necessary in administering nasal inhalation as long as the nurse will wait 30 minutes between puffs.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Administer the bronchodilator first, this is to relax the bronchial muscle and dilate the airway

When applying eye ointment, the following guidelines apply except:
1. Squeeze about 2 cm of ointment and gently close but not squeeze the eye
2. Apply the ointment from the inner canthus going outward of the affected eye
3. Discard the first bead of the eye ointment before application because the tube is likely to expel more than desire amount of ointment
4. Hold the tube above the conjunctival sac, do not let tip touch the conjunctiva
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Discard the first bead of the eye ointment before application because the tube is likely to expel more than desire amount of ointment

If you are to give 2 nasal inhalation for a client, one is a bronchodilator and the other one is a steroid, which guideline should you follow?
1. Administer the steroid first, this is to open the airway by lessening the edema
2. Administer the bronchodilator first, this is to relax the bronchial muscle and dilate the airway
3. Order is not necessary in administering nasal inhalation as long as that the nurse will wait 1 minute between administrations of 2 drugs
4. Order is not necessary in administering nasal inhalation as long as the nurse will wait 30 minutes between puffs
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Administer the bronchodilator first, this is to relax the bronchial muscle and dilate the airway

1. Right sidelying position

3. Supine position
4. Prone position

1. Right sidelying position

1. Mode
2. Standard deviation
3. Median
4. Frequency

>2. Standard deviation

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation

1. Superficial partial thickness burn
2. Deep partial thickness burn
3. Full thickness burn
4. Deep full thickness burn
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Full thickness burn

1. Structures beneath the skin are damage
2. Dermis is partially damaged
3. Epidermis and dermis are both damaged
4. Epidermis is damaged
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Dermis is partially damaged

1. Superficial partial thickness burn
2. Deep partial thickness burn
3. Full thickness burn
4. Deep full thickness burn

>2. Deep partial thickness burn

During the Acute phase of the burn injury, which of the following is a priority?
1. wound healing
2. reconstructive surgery
3. emotional support
4. fluid resuscitation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. wound healing

1. Prevent infection
2. Control pain
3. Prevent deformities and contractures
4. Return the hemodynamic stability via fluid resuscitation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Return the hemodynamic stability via fluid resuscitation

1. intramuscularly
2. subcutaneously
3. orally
4. intravenously
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. intravenously

1. irrigate with normal saline for 1 to 15 minutes
2. transport to a physician immediately
3. irrigate with water for 15 minutes or longer

>3. irrigate with water for 15 minutes or longer

1. stress ulcers
2. hemorrhage

4. hyperkalemia and hypernatremia
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. hyperkalemia and hyponatremia

1. Cerebral hypoxia
2. Hypervolemia
3. metabolic acidosis
4. Renal failure

4. For hyperkalemia

>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Below the expected weight.

A 6-month-old child returns from surgery. PRN orders are available for pain management. The nurse would administer the pain medication when the baby is observed:
1. Crying loudly, grimacing, restlessness.
2. Displaying a change of color, decreased temperature.
3. Demonstrating shortness of breath, lack of responsiveness.
4. Sleeping more, refusing to eat.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Crying loudly, grimacing, restlessness.

A mother of a 4-year-old tells the nurse that her son is a "picky eater." The nurse should inform the mother that she should:
1. Increase the amount of carbohydrates in the daily menu plan.
2. Administer vitamins twice a day to her child.
3. Be more concerned with the quantity of food than the quality of food.
4. Recognize this is common for preschoolers as their caloric requirements have decreased slightly.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Recognize this is common for preschoolers as their caloric requirements have decreased slightly

When examining the child, the nurse should remember that tonsillar tissue:
1. Enlarges until adolescence and then shrinks.
2. Continues to enlarge throughout childhood and adolescence.
3. Is readily visible in toddlers.
4. Normally has a small amount of exudate.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Enlarges until adolescence and then shrinks.

In discussing sexual maturation with a health class, the nurse would include the information that secondary sex characteristics begin to appear at:
1. 10 years in girls, 12 years in boys.
2. 12 years in girls, 16 years in boys.
3. 10 years in boys, 10 years in girls.
4. 12 years in girls and boys.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. 10 years in girls, 12 years in boys.

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Dave, 40 years old, came to the hospital for a diagnostic work-up for a cholelithiasis prior to surgery.

Which of the following clinical manifestations would you MOST likely to observe when a patient is suffering from Cholelithiasis?
1. Indigestion, pain on the right upper quadrant radiating pain to the shoulder
2. Vague left upper quadrant pain radiating to the scapula
3. Feeling of abdominal tenderness after waking-up in the morning
4. Feeling of abdominal fullness after taking meals
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Indigestion, pain on the right upper quadrant radiating pain to the shoulder

Which ONE of the following vitamins is interfered when there is obstruction of the bile flow in cholecystitis?
1. Vitamin C
2. Vitamin B
3. Vitamin B12
4. Vitamin K
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Vitamin K

The patient was ordered Endoscopic Retrograde Cholangiopancreatography (ERCP). He was put on a mild sedation. As a Nurse, what should you check as a PRIORITY action when he returns to the ward?
1. Irritation of oropharynx
2. Nausea and vomiting
3. cough and gag reflex
4. Signs of bleeding
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. cough and gag reflex

Which of the following conditions is NOT a side effect of anticholinergic drugs?
1. Constipation
2. Blurred vision
3. Dryness of the mouth
4. Increased blood pressure
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Increased blood pressure

When a client has a nasogastric tube (NGT) due to abdominal distention post surgery. Which of the following nursing responsibilities should you do? Select all that apply.
1. Measure gastric secretion every shift
2. Observe and record color, viscosity of secretions
3. Ensure that the gastric tube is patent
4. Assist patient to assume a comfortable position
A. 1, 2, 3, 4
B. 1, 2, 3
C. 1, 2
D. 2, 3, 4
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>A. 1, 2, 3, 4

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>The hospital director of a tertiary hospital is alarmed with the recent report of the head Human Resource Department Office (HRDO) that there is so much conflict going on among the health care professionals which is affecting quality patient care.

Which of the following is a form of dispute resolution and considered a legal technique which is outside the court?
1. Suppression
2. Arbitration
3. Bribe
4. Negotiation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Arbitration

Change is defined “as making something different from what it was”. If you become a unit manager in the future, which of the following is your FIRST step as an agent in promoting successful change in your health care setting?
1. Revisit Institutional Vision-Mission and adhere to its commitment
2. Obtain majority agreements when issues are presented
3. Include obsessed people as part of your Task force for change
4. Ignore organizational conflict as possible
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Revisit Institutional Vision-Mission and adhere to its commitment

Decision-making in an organizational structure comes at many levels. The level which is considered empowering to staff-member is when the unit manager does which one of the following?
1. Makes a decision when she reads the reported concerns
2. Ask direct report from personnel to decide on a solution
3. Makes a decision after convening a core group to analyze the concerned issues
4. Makes a decision by herself and assumes responsibility for her action
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Makes a decision after convening a core group to analyze the concerned issues

The nurse manager is receiving some feedback that one of her staff-nurses has been observed to be always irritated, “bossy”, and indifferent to her patients and some co-workers. Which of the following PRIORITY nursing actions should the manager implement?
1. Conduct a joint meeting of both parties involved
2. Request the concerned patients and co-workers to submit an Incident report
3. Call the nurse concerned and talk to her privately about the observations
4. Give a memo to the nurse involved
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Call the nurse concerned and talk to her privately about the observations

A team building session was conducted by the HRDO task force to come up with strategies for conflict resolution. Which of the following is a WIN-WIN approach in conflict management.
1. Each party involved agree to respond to majority vote
2. Each participants agree to resolve conflicts by adhering to the Institutional Vision and Mission
3. Each participants will give way to 60-40% of their agreements
4. Disagreements are settled with respective compromises on issues presented
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Each participants agree to resolve conflicts by adhering to the Institutional Vision and Mission

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Juvy, a retired Barangay Health Worker, came to the OPD for her check- up for her diabetes mellitus. She had been diabetic since she was 37 years old. She has been taking her maintenance medications which she sometimes does not comply with.

There are metabolic abnormalities in the development of type 2 Diabetes. Which of the following is NOT included in these abnormalities?
1. Inappropriate production of the liver
2. Increased ability of the pancreas to produce insulin
3. Insulin resistance
4. Altered production of hormones by adipose tissues
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Increased ability of the pancreas to produce insulin

Ms. Juvy was admitted to the hospital for further check-up. Which of the following diagnostic tests do you expect to be ordered by the diabetologist as an indicator that the patient is compliant to her prescribed diet?
1. Oral glucose tolerance test
2. Glycosylated hemoglobin level (hgb, Alc)
3. Finger glucose findings for one day
4. Fasting blood glucose level
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Glycosylated hemoglobin level (hgb, Alc)

While Nurse Ellen was completing her assessment, she discovered the following findings. Which of the following should she refer immediately to the physician?
1. Tingling sensation of the hands and feet
2. Changes in the peripheral vision
3. Beginning ulceration of the left big toe
4. Fruity odor breath
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Fruity odor breath

Nurse Ellen, the nurse in charge of patient Juvy, informed her physician that her serum glucose level is 38mmol/L and quite unresponsive to verbal questioning. The nurse suspects that she is starting to develop Diabetes Ketoacidosis (DKA). Which of the following manifestations is UNIQUE to this condition?
1. Shallow slow respirations
2. Increased serum potassium
3. Rapid deep respirations
4. Decreased serum albumin
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Rapid deep respirations

Nurse Ellen’s counseling role includes lifestyle changes as well as pharmacologic regimen. Juvy’s family were interested to know information regarding insulin. She differentiated an intermediate acting insulin from that of short-acting which is:
1. Regular onset is 2 hrs. Peak is 3 ½ hr., duration -7 hrs., administered 20-30 min. before meal
2. Regular onset is 2-4 hr., peak is 4-12 hr., duration is 8 hr., administered 20-30 min. after meal
3. Regular, onset is 1 ½ hr, peak is 3-4 hrs, duration is 6 hrs. administered 20-30 min after meal
4. Regular onset is 1 ½ - 1hr, peak is 2-3 hr., 4-6hr duration administered 20-30 min. before
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Regular onset is 1 ½ - 1hr, peak is 2-3 hr., 4-6hr duration administered 20-30 min. before

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Nurse Mich admitted Aileen, 38 years old, who was diagnosed by her physician with Type I Diabetes Mellitus. She complains of easy fatigability and increased tiredness. Nurse Mich, during the assessment, noted the presence of a foot ulcer which Aileen was trying to hide.

Nurse Mich holds the hands of Aileen while doing her assessment. Her hands were cold and clammy, she suspected that the patient was having hypoglycemia. To relieve her condition, an immediate action is to offer her:
1. Candy
2. Full meal
3. Sandwich
4. Fruits
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Candy

Nurse Mich watches Ms. Aileen while sleeping. An EXCELLENT guideline to differentiate if a patient is just sleeping or experiencing hypoglycemic reaction is when one is observed to be:
1. With dyspnea
2. Snoring
3. With diaphoresis
4. Grunting his teeth
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. With diaphoresis

Nurse Mich practiced surgical asepsis during foot care. Which of the following techniques has to be observed?
1. Opening container of sterile water after putting gloves on.
2. Changing the sterile field after sterile water spilled on it
3. Placing sterile dressing 2 cm from the edge of the sterile field. 1 CM
4. Cleaning the wound in circular motion from outer towards the ulcer site
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Changing the sterile field after sterile water spilled on it

Nurse Mich after foot care encourages Patient Aileen to do which of the following APPROPRIATE measures?
1. Apply lanolin generously between the toes
2. Cut toenails rounded at the edges and close to the skin
3. Apply alcohol after cleansing feet to improve infection
4. Wear a shoe-type slipper at home
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Wear a shoe-type slipper at home

Ms. Aileen was administered NPH insulin at 8 am. At what time would Nurse Mich expect the patient to be at risk for hypoglycemic reaction?
1. 11 am
2. Noon
3. 6 pm
4. 4 pm
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Noon

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation

2. Change the boy’s street clothes to surgical gown
3. Shave the operative site
4. Call the OR nurse for scheduling

The boy is transferred to the operating room. What is the BEST mode to be used in transferring the patient?
1. Nurses’ carry
2. Stretcher
3. mother’s carry
4. wheelchair

>2. Stretcher

1. Hypoventilation
2. Hyperventilation
3. Hypothermia
4. Hyperthermia

>3. Hypothermia

2. “It is the doctor's order; you’ll have to accept the situation.”
3. “Your child’s condition is an emergency case. If he is not operated on, he will die.”

>4. “I understand your feelings, but your child needs to be operated on.”

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>There are extensive legal aspects that guide the Filipino nurses in terms of regulation in practice of her profession.

The Professional Regulation Commission, Board of Nursing (PRC– BoN) as a regulatory board has the legal functions and responsibilities EXCEPT in ONE of the following:
1. Ensure the quality nursing education by jointly monitoring with the Commission on Higher Education (CHED) adherence to its guidelines, policies and standards
2. Monitor and enforce quality standards and nursing practice in the Philippines to ensure efficient, ethical, moral, technical professional standards
3. Issue, suspend or revoke certificates of registration for the practice of nursing
4. Recognize specialty organizations in coordination with the accredited professional organization and collect fees to upgrade the conditions of Nurses
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Recognize specialty organizations in coordination with the accredited professional organization and collect fees to upgrade the conditions of Nurses

You are a nurse in Las Pinas Doctors Hospital and have just completed a 2 year experience in the surgical unit. One day, your supervisor ordered you to go on a float to the Intensive Care Unit (ICU) as two of the nurses called “on sick” in the said unit. What is the MOST important action you should do in this situation?
1. Explain to your supervisor that you might not be able to perform safely your duty as a nurse in the unit
2. File a leave instead and call your husband to fetch you in the hospital
3. Refuse the order and tell your supervisor your don’t want to put your license in jeopardy
4. Report to the surgical ward of your assignment and request one of your nurses to replace you instead as floater in the ICU.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Explain to your supervisor that you might not be able to perform safely your duty as a nurse in the unit

Janna, a 35-year old, married to an insurance agent, was diagnosed with colon cancer only a month ago. The couple have very limited information about this condition. One day, you saw the husband in the room reading the chart which was inadvertently left by a medical intern. What PRIORITY Nursing actions should you do in this situation?
1. Get the chart from the husband so he will not be able to read the diagnosis of his wife
2. Explain to the husband as per policy, relatives are not allowed to read the chart
3. Report immediately to the supervisor on duty and submit an incident report
4. Ask the husband what information he would like to ask from the health care professional regarding medical plan and diagnosis
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Ask the husband what information he would like to ask from the health care professional regarding medical plan and diagnosis

Nurse Nicole, is assisting Mr. Caca who just came from the Recovery unit for a thoracic surgery. She noted that the dressings are saturated with blood, but the Surgeon just reassured the Nurse to reinforce the dressings and monitor him closely. After an hour, Mr. Caca went into shock and died. The family filed charges against the Doctor and the Nurse. What is the lawsuit involved in this case?
1. Murder
2. Assault
3. Battery
4. Malpractice
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Malpractice

What is the MOST important Nursing measure that Nurse Nicole should have done to avoid this situation? Select all that apply.
1. Monitor and record closely the vital signs until stable
2. Report to the surgeon the vital signs and degree of bleeding from operative site
3. Call the supervisor on duty to assist you in referring the patient to the surgeon
4. Ask the family members to call the surgeon to see the patient
A. 2, 3
B. 1, 2, 3
C. 1, 2
D. 1, 3
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>B. 1, 2, 3

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Honey, 23 year old, a dental student has been having frequent bouts of tonsillitis in the past. One day, she developed low grade fever, dyspnea, dizziness, syncope, and fainting spells while preparing for her final examination. She was rushed to the hospital by her parents and was seen in the Emergency room by the physician on duty (POD), Ms. Jenny was the nurse-on-duty. The POD ordered a 12 lead Electro-cardiogram (EKG) and other laboratory tests.

What specific information is essential for the Health professionals to know when this EKG is ordered for patient Honey?
1. Rate, rhythm and pressure within the blood vessels
2. Rate, rhythm, axis and circulation
3. Rate, rhythm, axis, hypertrophy, and infarction
4. Rate, hypertrophy and blockage to the chambers of the heart
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Rate, rhythm, axis, hypertrophy, and infarction

Aside from the EKG and laboratory studies, the POD ordered patient Honey to undergo cardiac catheterization to establish further the medical diagnosis of Valvular heart disease. Which of the following is NOT true as part of Nurse Jenny instructions to the patient regarding this procedure?
1. Signing of consent is optional
2. Normal procedure is less than 2 hours
3. Fasting should be 8 to 12 hours
4. Presence of pounding sensation in the chest during the procedure
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Signing of consent is optional

Nurse Jenny must be alert that certain complications may arise after the procedure. What PRIORITY nursing assessment should she observe?
1. Tingling sensation
2. Signs of bleeding at the puncture site
3. Blurring vision
4. Disorientation
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Signs of bleeding at the puncture site

When teaching patient Honey about self-management following cardiac catheterization, Nurse Jenny should emphasize to AVOID which ONE of the following?
1. Diet high in Protein and Carbohydrates to low cholesterol and fats
2. Lifting objects heavier than five (5) lbs
3. Taking shower with the site covered after 24 hours
4. Light exercise program within 48 hours when tolerated
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Taking shower with the site covered after 24 hours

The POD established Honey’s diagnosis that she is suffering from acquired valvular heart disease. This condition is brought about by:
1. Rheumatic fever
2. Drug abuse
3. alcohol consumption
4. heredity
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Rheumatic fever

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>After an abdominal surgery, the circulating and scrub nurses have critical responsibility about sponge and instrument count.

Counting is performed thrice: During the pre-incision phase, the operative phase and closing phase. Who counts the sponges, needles and instruments?
1. The scrub nurse only
2. The circulating nurse only
3. The surgeon and the assistant surgeon
4. The scrub nurse and the circulating nurse
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The scrub nurse and the circulating nurse

The layer of the abdomen is divided into five layers. Arrange the following from the first layer going to the deepest layer:
1. Skin, Subcutaneous/Fat, Peritoneum, Muscle, Fascia
2. Skin, Subcutaneous/Fat, Fascia, Peritoneum, Muscle
3. Skin, Subcutaneous/Fat, Muscle, Fascia, Peritoneum
4. Skin, Subcutaneous/Fat, Fascia, Muscle, Peritoneum
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Skin, Subcutaneous/Fat, Fascia, Muscle, Peritoneum

When is the first sponge/instrument count reported?
1. Before closing the subcutaneous layer
2. Before peritoneum is closed
3. Before closing the skin
4. Before the fascia is sutured
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Before peritoneum is closed

Like any nursing interventions, counts should be documented. To whom does the scrub nurse report any discrepancy of counts so that immediate and appropriate action is instituted?
1. Anesthesiologists
2. Surgeon
3. OR nurse supervisor
4. Circulating nurse
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Surgeon

Which of the following are 2 interventions of the surgical team when an instrument was confirmed missing?
1. MRI and Incidence report
2. CT Scan, MRI, Incidence report
3. X-ray and Incidence report
4. CT Scan and Incidence report
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. X-ray and Incidence report

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>An entry level nurse should be able to apply theoretical knowledge in the performance of the basic nursing skills.

A client has an indwelling urinary catheter and she is suspected of having urinary infection. How should you collect a urine specimen for culture and sensitivity?
1. Clamp tubing for 60 minutes and insert a sterile needle into the tubing above the clamp to aspirate urine
2. Drain urine from the drainage bag into the sterile container
3. Disconnect the tubing from the urinary catheter and let urine flow into a sterile container
4. Wipe the self-sealing aspiration port with antiseptic solution and insert a sterile needle into the self-sealing port
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Wipe the self-sealing aspiration port with antiseptic solution and insert a sterile needle into the self-sealing port

To obtain specimen for sputum culture and sensitivity, which of the following instruction is best?
1. Upon waking up, cough deeply and expectorate into container
2. Cough after pursed lip breathing
3. Save sputum for two days in covered container
4. After respiratory treatment, expectorate into a container
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Upon waking up, cough deeply and expectorate into container

The best time for collecting the sputum specimen for culture and sensitivity is:
1. Before retiring at night
2. Anytime of the day
3. Upon waking up in the morning
4. Before meals
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Upon waking up in the morning

When suctioning the endotracheal tube, the nurse should:
1. Explain procedure to patient; insert catheter gently applying suction. Withdrawn using twisting motion
2. Insert catheter until resistance is met, and then withdraw slightly, applying suction intermittently as catheter is withdrawn
3. Hyperoxygenate client insert catheter using back and forth motion
4. Insert suction catheter four inches into the tube, suction 30 seconds using a twirling motion as the catheter is withdrawn
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Insert catheter until resistance is met, and then withdraw slightly, applying suction intermittently as catheter is withdrawn

The purpose of NGT IMMEDIATELY after an operation is:
1. For feeding or gavage
2. For gastric decompression
3. For lavage, or the cleansing of the stomach content
4. For the rapid return of peristalsis
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. For gastric decompression

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Mr. Santos, 50, is to undergo cystoscopy due to multiple problems like scantly urination, hematuria and dysuria.

You are the nurse in charge in Mr. Santos. When asked what are the organs to be examined during cystoscopy, you will enumerate as follows:
1. Urethra, kidney, bladder, urethra
2. Urethra, bladder wall, trigone, ureteral opening
3. Bladder wall, uterine wall, and urethral opening
4. Urethral opening, ureteral opening bladder
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Urethra, bladder wall, trigone, ureteral opening

In the OR, you will position Mr. Santos who is cystoscopy in:
1. Supine
2. Lithotomy
3. Semi-fowler
4. Trendelenburg
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Lithotomy

After cystoscopy, Mr. Santos asked you to explain why there is no incision of any kind. What do you tell him?
1. “Cystoscopy is direct visualization and examination by urologist”.
2. “Cystoscopy is done by x-ray visualization of the urinary tract”.
3. “Cystoscopy is done by using lasers on the urinary tract”.
4. “Cystoscopy is an endoscopic procedure of the urinary tract”.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. “Cystoscopy is an endoscopic procedure of the urinary tract”.

Within 24-48 hours post cystoscopy, it is normal to observe one the following:
1. Pink-tinged urine
2. Distended bladder
3. Signs of infection
4. Prolonged hematuria
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Pink-tinged urine

Leg cramps are NOT uncommon post cystoscopy. Nursing intervention includes:
1. Bed rest
2. Warm moist soak
3. Early ambulation
4. Hot sitz bath
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Warm moist soak

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Felix, a 79 year old man who is brought to the Surgical Unit from PACU after a transurethral resection. You are assigned to receive him. You noted that he has a 3-way indwelling urinary catheter for continuous fast drip bladder irrigation which is connected to a straight drainage.

Immediately after surgery, what would you expect his urine to be?
1. Light yellow
2. Bright red
3. Amber
4. Pinkish to red
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Pinkish to red

The purpose of the continuous bladder irrigation is to:
1. Allow continuous monitoring of the fluid output status
2. Provide continuous flushing of clots and debris from the bladder
3. Allow for proper exchange of electrolytes and fluid
4. Ensure accurate monitoring of intake and output
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Provide continuous flushing of clots and debris from the bladder

Felix informs you that he feels some discomfort on the hypogastric area and he has to void. What will be your most appropriate action?
1. Remove his catheter then allow him to void on his own
2. Irrigate his catheter
3. Tell him to “Go ahead and void. You have an indwelling catheter.”
4. Assess color and rate of outflow, if there is changes refer to urologist for possible irrigation.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Assess color and rate of outflow, if there is changes refer to urologist for possible irrigation.

1. Phlebitis
2. Infiltration to subcutaneous tissue
3. Pyrogenic reaction
4. Air embolism
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Infiltration to subcutaneous tissue

Knowing that proper documentation of assessment findings and interventions are important responsibilities of the nurse during first post-operative day, which of the following is the LEAST relevant to document in the case of Felix?
1. Chest pain and vital signs
2. Intravenous infusion rate
3. Amount, color, and consistency of bladder irrigation drainage
4. Activities of daily living started
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Activities of daily living started

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Melamine contamination in milk has brought worldwide crisis both in the milk production sector as well as the health and economy. Being aware of the current events is one quality that a nurse should possess to prove that nursing is a dynamic profession that will adapt depending on the patient’s needs.

Melamine is a synthetic resin used for whiteboards, hard plastics and jewelry box covers due to its fire retardant properties. Milk and food manufacturers add melamine in order to:
1. It has a bacteriostatic property leading to increase food and milk life as a way of preserving the foods
2. Gives a glazy and more edible look on foods
3. Make milks more tasty and creamy
4. Create an illusion of a high protein content on their products
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Create an illusion of a high protein content on their products

Most of the milks contaminated by Melamine came from which country?
1. India
2. China
3. Philippines
4. Korea
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. China

Which government agency is responsible for testing the melamine content of foods and food products?
1. DOH
2. MMDA
3. NBI
4. BFAD
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. BFAD

Infants are the most vulnerable to melamine poisoning. Which of the following is NOT a sign of melamine poisoning?
1. Irritability, Back ache, Urolithiasis
2. High blood pressure, fever
3. Anuria, Oliguria or Hematuria
4. Fever, Irritability and a large output of diluted urine
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Fever, Irritability and a large output of diluted urine

What kind of renal failure will melamine poisoning cause?
1. Chronic, Prerenal
2. Chronic, Intrarenal
3. Acute, Postrenal
4. Acute, Prerenal
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. Acute, Postrenal

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Leukemia is the most common type of childhood cancer. Acute Lymphoid Leukemia is the cause of almost 1/3 of all cancer that occurs in children under age 15.

The survival rate for Acute Lymphoid Leukemia is approximately:
1. 25%
2. 40%
3. 75%
4. 95%
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. 75%

Whereas acute non-lymphoid leukemia has a survival rate of:
1. 25%
2. 40%
3. 75%
4. 95%
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. 40%

The three main consequence of leukemia that cause the most danger is:
1. Neutropenia causing infection, anemia causing impaired oxygenation and thrombocytopenia leading to bleeding tendencies
2. Central nervous system infiltration, anemia causing impaired oxygenation and thrombocytopenia leading to bleeding tendencies
3. Splenomegaly, hepatomegaly, fractures
4. Invasion by the leukemic cells to the bone causing severe bone pain
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Neutropenia causing infection, anemia causing impaired oxygenation and thrombocytopenia leading to bleeding tendencies

Gold standard in the diagnosis of leukemia is by which of the following?
1. Blood culture and sensitivity
2. Bone marrow biopsy
3. Blood biopsy
4. CSF aspiration and examination
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Bone marrow biopsy

Adriamycin, Vincristine, Prednisone and L asparaginase are given to the client for long term therapy. One common side effect, especially of adriamycin is alopecia. The child asks: “Will I get my hair back once again?” The nurse best respond is by saying:
1. “Don’t be silly, ofcourse you will get your hair back”
2. “We are not sure, let’s hope it’ll grow”
3. “This side effect is usually permanent, but I will get the doctor to discuss it for you”
4. “Your hair will regrow in 3 to 6 months but of different color, usually darker and of different texture”
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. “Your hair will regrow in 3 to 6 months but of different color, usually darker and of different texture”

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Breast Cancer is the 2nd most common type of cancer after lung cancer and 99% of which, occurs in woman. Survival rate is 98% if this is detected early and treated promptly. Carmen is a 53 year old patient in the high risk group for breast cancer was recently diagnosed with Breast cancer.

All of the following are factors that said to contribute to the development of breast cancer except:
1. Prolonged exposure to estrogen such as an early menarche or late menopause, nulliparity and childbirth after age 30
2. Genetics
3. Increasing Age
4. Prolonged intake of Tamoxifen (Nolvadex)
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Prolonged intake of Tamoxifen (Nolvadex)

Protective factors for the development of breast cancer includes which of the following except:
1. Exercise
2. Breast feeding
3. Prophylactic Tamoxifen
4. Alcohol intake
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Alcohol intake

A patient diagnosed with breast cancer has been offered the treatment choices of breast conservation surgery with radiation or a modified radical mastectomy. When questioned by the patient about these options, the nurse informs the patient that the lumpectomy with radiation:
1. Reduces the fear and anxiety that accompany the diagnosis and treatment of cancer
2. Has about the same 10-year survival rate as the modified radical mastectomy
3. Provides a shorter treatment period with a fewer long term complications
4. Preserves the normal appearance and sensitivity of the breast.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Preserves the normal appearance and sensitivity of the breast.

Carmen, who is asking the nurse the most appropriate time of the month to do her self-examination of the breast. The MOST appropriate reply by the nurse would be:
1. The 26th day of the menstrual cycle
2. 7 to 8 days after conclusion of the menstrual period
3. During her menstruation
4. The same day each month
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. 7 to 8 days after conclusion of the menstrual period

Carmen being treated with radiation therapy. What should be included in the plan of care to minimize skin damage from the radiation therapy?
1. Cover the areas with thick clothing materials
2. Apply a heating pad to the site
3. Wash skin with water after the therapy
4. Avoid applying creams and powders to the area
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. Avoid applying creams and powders to the area

Based on the DOH and World Health Organization (WHO) guidelines, the mainstay for early detection method for breast cancer that is recommended for developing countries is:
1. A monthly breast self-examination (BSE) and an annual health worker breast examination (HWBE)
2. An annual hormone receptor assay
3. An annual mammogram
4. A physician conduct a breast clinical examination every 2 years
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. A monthly breast self-examination (BSE) and an annual health worker breast examination (HWBE)

1. Fibrocystic masses

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation
>Budgeting is an important part of a nurse managerial activity. The correct allocation and distribution of resources is vital in the harmonious operation of the financial balance of the agency.

1. Plan for the allocation of resources for future use
2. The process of allocating resources for future use
3. Estimate cost of expenses
4. Continuous process in seeing that the goals and objective of the agency is met
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Plan for the allocation of resources for future use

Which of the following best defines Capital Budget?
1. Budget to estimate the cost of direct labor, number of staff to be hired and necessary number of workers to meet the general patient needs
2. Includes the monthly and daily expenses and expected revenue and expenses
3. These are related to long term planning and includes major replacement or expansion of the plant, major equipment and inventories.
4. These are expenses that are not dependent on the level of production or sales. They tend to be time-related, such as salaries or rents being paid per month
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. These are related to long term planning and includes major replacement or expansion of the plant, major equipment and inventories.

Which of the following best described Operational Budget?
1. Budget to estimate the cost of direct labor, number of staff to be hired and necessary number of workers to meet the general patient needs
2. Includes the monthly and daily expenses and expected revenue and expenses
3. These are related to long term planning and includes major replacement or expansion of the plant, major equipment and inventories.
4. These are expenses that are not dependent on the level of production or sales. They tend to be time-related, such as rent
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. Includes the monthly and daily expenses and expected revenue and expenses

Which of the following accurately describes a Fixed Cost in budgeting?
1. These are usually the raw materials and labor salaries that depend on the production or sales
2. These are expenses that change in proportion to the activity of a business
3. These are expenses that are not dependent on the level of production or sales. They tend to be time-related, such as rent
4. This is the summation of the Variable Cost and the Fixed Cost
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>3. These are expenses that are not dependent on the level of production or sales. They tend to be time-related, such as rent

Which of the following accurately describes Variable Cost in budgeting?
1. These are related to long term planning and include major replacement or expansion of the plant, major equipment and inventories.
2. These are expenses that change in proportion to the activity of a business
3. These are expenses that are not dependent on the level of production or sales. They tend to be time-related, such as rent
4. This is the summation of the Variable Cost and the Fixed Cost
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>2. These are expenses that change in proportion to the activity of a business

>[!EXAMPLE] Situation

You know that apnea is seen in client’s with Cheyne stokes respiration, APNEA is defined as:
1. Inability to breathe in a supine position so the patient sits up in bed to breathe
2. The patient is dead, the breathing stops
3. There is an absence of breathing for a period of time, usually 15 seconds or more
4. A period of hypercapnia and hypoxia due to the cessation of respiratory effort in spite of normal respiratory functioning
>[!FAQ]- Answer

Following spinal injury, the nurse should encourage the client to drink fuids to avoid:
1. Urinary tract infection.
2. Fluid and electrolyte imbalance.
3. Dehydration.
4. Skin breakdown.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>1. Clients in the early stage of spinal cord damage experience an atonic bladder, which is characterized by the absence of muscle tone, an enlarged capacity, no feeling of discomfort with distention, and overfow with a large residual. This leads to urinary stasis and infection. High fuid intake limits urinary stasis and infection by diluting the urine and increasing urinary output.

The client is transferred from the operating room to recovery room after an open-heart surgery. The nurse assigned is taking the vital signs of the client. The nurse notifed the physician when the temperature of the client rises to 38.8ºC or 102ºF because elevated temperatures:
1. May be a forerunner of hemorrhage.
2. Are related to diaphoresis and possible chilling.
3. May indicate cerebral edema.
4. Increase the cardiac output.
>[!FAQ]- Answer
>4. The temperature of 102 ºF (38.8ºC) or greater lead to an increased metabolism and cardiac workload.
